Quel est le plan de transition pour l'atténuation du changement climatique ? Pour répondre à cette question, nous souhaitons avoir une description brève des principaux leviers de décarbonation, du plan d'investissement et de financement du plan de transition, et de la comptabilité avec un scénario 1,5°C ou 2°C.

Parmi les informations que nous recherchons, nous pouvons lister les éléments suivants :

Plan de transition est aligné avec un scénario 1,5°C.

Leviers de décarbonation programmés.

Plan d'investissement et de financement des leviers de décarbonation.

Alignement de la stratégie et le plan de financement.

Suivi des progrès.

    Résumé du contenu du tableau : - Les émissions totales de CO2e provenant des investissements (tCO2e) ont diminué de manière significative entre 2023 (678,379 tCO2e) et 2024 (505,085 tCO2e). Cette baisse est observée à la fois dans la gestion d'actifs et le portefeuille propriétaire. - Les émissions par DKKm montrent également une réduction entre 2023 et 2024, passant de 8.6 à 6.1 tCO2e par DKKm. - En 2024, les émissions de la gestion d'actifs (265,769 tCO2e) sont légèrement supérieures à celles du portefeuille propriétaire (239,316 tCO2e), mais les deux catégories ont connu une baisse par rapport à 2023. - Les émissions par DKKm pour la gestion d'actifs et le portefeuille propriétaire ont également diminué en 2024, atteignant respectivement 5.5 et 6.9.

Le plan de transition pour l'atténuation du changement climatique de Spar Nord est décrit dans plusieurs documents. Voici un résumé des principaux éléments :

  1. Alignement avec un scénario 1,5°C : Spar Nord s'est engagé à atteindre la neutralité carbone d'ici 2050, en ligne avec l'objectif de l'Accord de Paris de limiter le réchauffement climatique à 2°C au-dessus des niveaux préindustriels, avec une ambition d'atteindre 1,5°C. Les objectifs de réduction sont fondés sur les scénarios scientifiques basés sur les trajectoires de réduction du Groupe d'experts intergouvernemental sur l'évolution du climat (IPCC).

  2. Leviers de décarbonation programmés : Le plan de transition met l'accent sur la décabornisation des actifs et activités des clients. Spar Nord vise à réduire les émissions financées de son portefeuille de prêts, avec un objectif de réduction de 50% des émissions financées par rapport à un niveau de référence de 2021 d'ici 2030. Cela inclut des initiatives telles que le financement de voitures électriques et la transition vers des technologies à faibles émissions.

  3. Plan d'investissement et de financement : Le rôle de Spar Nord en tant qu'institution financière est de faciliter les flux de capitaux vers des solutions technologiques et des modèles commerciaux favorables au climat. Le plan d'investissement met l'accent sur le financement de la transition des secteurs clés émetteurs de GES vers des technologies à faibles émissions ou zéro émission.

  4. Alignement de la stratégie et le plan de financement : La stratégie de Spar Nord pour 2023-2025 est axée sur la contribution à une société durable et neutre en carbone. Cela inclut l'amélioration continue de la transparence des objectifs climatiques et des actions pour garantir que les réductions d'émissions reflètent les progrès réels.

  5. Suivi des progrès : Spar Nord s'engage à améliorer constamment son reporting et à augmenter la transparence de ses objectifs climatiques et actions. Cela implique de revoir continuellement ses objectifs, actions et priorités en matière de durabilité et de responsabilité sociale, tout en s'appuyant sur la recherche et l'analyse pour améliorer la qualité des données.

En résumé, le plan de transition de Spar Nord est bien structuré pour aligner ses efforts de décarbonation avec les objectifs climatiques internationaux, tout en jouant un rôle actif dans le financement de la transition vers une économie à faible émission de carbone.

  • La tabla detalla la organización y resultados del compromiso de Spar Nord con grupos de interés internos y externos en 2024. Los grupos internos incluyen el Consejo de Administración, la Junta Ejecutiva, el grupo de dirección ESG, el Comité de Inversión Responsable, el Comité de Finanzas Sostenibles y los empleados, con actividades como reuniones trimestrales, talleres y consultas, enfocadas en metas de sostenibilidad, gobernanza y desarrollo de productos responsables. Las metas están vinculadas a ESRS E1 y S1, y se alinean con la estrategia y modelo de negocio del banco.
  • impacts, risks and opportunities. In identifying cli- mate-related transition events and substantiat- ing the Bank's targets for El Climate change, sci- entific scenarios have been used. These scenarios use reduction pathways from the UN's Intergov- ernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPPC), which are consistent across the Bank's impact areas. The IPCC prepares reduction pathways based on the latest climate science and comprehensive analyses of global data. These pathways take into account complex climate interactions, socio- economic factors and technological advances. Spar Nord has chosen the IPCC's reduction path- ways to ensure that climate objectives are scien- tifically substantiated, ambitious and in line with international commitments. They also provide a common frame of reference that makes it easier to understand Spar Nord's climate ambitions in both a national and global context.
  • % 100 80 60 40 20 0 2020 20242025 2030 Spar Nord Target IPCC pathway In 2024, financed emissions from investments in equities and corporate bonds in asset manage- ment, including investments in the asset classes through unit trust certificates, were reduced by 48% compared to the 2020 baseline. In 2024, fi- nanced emissions thus amounted to 5.9 tCO2e per DKK million. The positive developments in 2024 were attributa- ble in particular to lower financed emissions from investments in corporate bonds, which related both to conversion to more climate-friendly unit trust certificates and a reduction in emissions from existing unit trust certificates. The reduction means that the Bank has met the sub-target for 2025 and is well on its way to- wards meeting the 2030 target.
  • ## Financial reporting ### Targets To support the realisation of Spar Nord's climate ambition of net zero by 2050, we have defined a number of 2030 sub-targets for decarbonisation of loan and investment activities and for the Bank's own operations. Additionally, Spar Nord has set sub-targets for selected segments, accompanied by specific actions and metrics, all designed to support the Bank's strategic direction. The reduction targets and sub-targets defined by the Bank are based on baseline analyses of the Bank's climate footprint through scope 1, 2 and 3. As the Bank's climate change initiatives are an on- going process, the baseline years are not identical across the three impact areas. However, the 2050 ambition is shared across the entire business, just as all activities have been assigned sub-targets for decarbonisation by 2030. Spar Nord's targets have been substantiated using scientific scenarios, which are described in more detail under the spe- cific activity.
  • The reduction targets for financed emissions from the Bank's core activities of loans and investments relate to significant shares of the Bank's business volume for bank and leasing loans and invest- ments in equities and corporate bonds in the Bank's asset management. The reduction targets related to the Bank's core activities are calculated in the relative metric tCO2e per DKK million, while the reduction targets for own operations are calculated in absolute emissions in the tCO2e metric. The illustration gives an overview of the Bank's cli- mate-related targets. For each target, the base- line years and the sub-targets set for 2025 and 2030 are presented. The target achievement by the end of 2024 illustrates progress relative to the Bank's 2030 targets measured on the basis of the relevant baseline year.
  • ## Group management's report Financial reporting ### Climate plan In 2024, Spar Nord prepared a climate plan, which is the Bank's version of the transition plan for cli- mate change mitigation. The climate plan has been approved by the Executive Board and Board of Directors of the Bank.
  • may happen that both we and our customers com- pensate for the same GHG emissions, which will lead to potential double compensation. However, this does not change the fact that Spar Nord con- siders its climate ambition and targets to be sig- nificant and important, as we, as a financial insti- tution, play a central role in driving financing and investments towards a low carbon economy. Our climate ambition therefore also relates to an am- bition to continuously improve our reporting and increase the transparency of our climate targets and actions to ensure that emission reductions re- flect actual progress. Spar Nord is aware of that science and legislation in the sustainability area are constantly evolving, which is why we maintain a fact-based approach in our climate change mitigation efforts. We do this by focusing on research and analysis, working proactively to improve data quality, and continu- ously reviewing our goals, actions, and priorities.
  • ### Climate actions and resources The work on implementing the climate plan is an- chored in a governance structure with clearly de- fined roles and responsibilities. Where strategy and ambition are anchored with the Bank's Board of Directors and Executive Board, the ESG steering group evaluates ongoing efforts to ensure pro- gress on the Bank's climate ambition. Spar Nord's committee for responsible investment and committee for sustainable finance recom- mend and prioritise concrete actions for the execu- tion of the Bank's climate-related targets and sub-targets. Read more about dedicated sustainability resources in the section on ESRS 2 Sustainability governance.

Furthermore, the Bank has set a target of reducing scope 3 GHG emissions from own operations by 25% by 2030 compared to the 2021 baseline of 24,748 tCO2e. Spar Nord has opted to substanti- ate its targets based on the IPCC reduction path- way.

Les éléments spécifiques tels que les leviers de décarbonation programmés, le plan d'investissement et de financement, ainsi que l'alignement avec un scénario 1,5°C ou 2°C ne sont pas explicitement détaillés dans les contextes disponibles.

E1-5

Les objectifs de réduction fixés sont-ils alignés avec une trajectoire de 1,5°C conformément aux Accords de Paris ? L'entreprise mentionne-t-elle une trajectoire conforme aux objectifs SBTi ? Il convient également de noter que, si l'entreprise affiche des objectifs de neutralité carbone, cette neutralité doit nécessairement être alignée avec les recommandations de l'Accord de Paris.

Pour garantir la compatibilité avec un scénario de transition conforme à l'accord de Paris, l'entreprise doit fournir les informations suivantes :

- Un/des objectif(s) de réduction avec une trajectoire de réchauffement à 1,5°C grâce à une trajectoire de décarbonation sectorielle si disponible, soit grâce à une trajectoire d'émissions transsectorielle compatible avec la limitation de réchauffement de la planète à 1,5°C (cf. AR 26 et 27).

- Les facteurs de réduction des émissions évoluent et ne sont pas fixes encore. Par conséquent, les entreprises sont encouragées à n'utiliser que des informations actualisées et publiquement accessibles. L'EFRAG préconise Pathways to Net-Zero - SBTi Technical Summary). Les cibles de réduction doivent être fixées respectivement à 2030 et 2050, avec des échellons tous les 5 ans.

Je ne dispose pas des informations nécessaires dans les documents fournis pour déterminer si les objectifs de réduction de l'entreprise sont alignés avec une trajectoire de 1,5°C conformément aux Accords de Paris ou si l'entreprise mentionne une trajectoire conforme aux objectifs SBTi. Les informations concernant une trajectoire de réchauffement à 1,5°C ou l'utilisation de trajectoires de décarbonation spécifiques ne sont pas explicitement mentionnées dans les contextes disponibles. Si l'entreprise affiche des objectifs de neutralité carbone, ces derniers doivent être alignés avec les recommandations de l'Accord de Paris, mais cette information n'est pas précisée dans les documents fournis.

    • L'axe horizontal indique les années, de 2023 à 2030.
    • Trois courbes sont tracées :
    • Une ligne rouge représentant "Spar Nord", qui reste stable à environ 80 % entre 2023 et 2024.
    • Une ligne noire en pointillés intitulée "Target", qui diminue progressivement de 80 % en 2023 à 0 % en 2030.
    • Une ligne grise en pointillés intitulée "CRREM pathway", qui suit une trajectoire descendante plus douce, partant de 100 % en 2023 pour atteindre environ 20 % en 2030.

Targets for decarbonisation of own operations Spar Nord is focused on mitigating the environ- mental and climate impact of the Bank’s own ac- tivities, for example by proactively promoting en- vironmental responsibility and sustainable tech- nologies in relevant areas of its operations. To support Spar Nord’s aspirations of net zero by 2050, the Bank has set a goal of reducing scope 1 and 2 GHG emissions by 30% by 2025 and 50% by 2030 compared to the 2021 baseline of 681 tCO2e. The reduction means that the Bank has met the sub-target for 2025 and is well on its way to- wards meeting the 2030 target. To support Spar Nord’s aspirations of net zero by 2050, the Bank has set a goal of reducing scope 1 and 2 GHG emissions by 30% by 2025 and 50% by 2030 compared to the 2021 baseline of 681 tCO2e. Les informations fournies indiquent que Spar Nord a fixé des objectifs de réduction des émissions de gaz à effet de serre alignés sur les scénarios de réduction basés sur la science, en particulier ceux émanant du Groupe d'experts intergouvernemental sur l'évolution du climat (IPCC). L'entreprise a un objectif ambitieux de neutralité carbone d'ici 2050, avec des sous-objectifs pour 2030. Ces objectifs sont alignés avec l'Accord de Paris, qui vise à limiter le réchauffement climatique à 1,5°C au-dessus des niveaux préindustriels.

Spar Nord a également spécifiquement mentionné l'application d'une trajectoire de réduction de l'IPCC qui implique une réduction minimale de 48% des émissions de GES d'ici 2030. Cela suggère que l'entreprise s'efforce de respecter les recommandations de l'Accord de Paris et les objectifs de SBTi (Science Based Targets initiative), bien que ces derniers ne soient pas explicitement mentionnés dans les contextes fournis.

L'entreprise a défini des échelons de réduction des émissions avec des objectifs intermédiaires pour 2025 et 2030, ce qui est en ligne avec les recommandations d'avoir des échelons tous les 5 ans pour suivre les progrès vers la neutralité carbone.

  • La tabla detalla la organización y resultados del compromiso de Spar Nord con grupos de interés internos y externos en 2024. Los grupos internos incluyen el Consejo de Administración, la Junta Ejecutiva, el grupo de dirección ESG, el Comité de Inversión Responsable, el Comité de Finanzas Sostenibles y los empleados, con actividades como reuniones trimestrales, talleres y consultas, enfocadas en metas de sostenibilidad, gobernanza y desarrollo de productos responsables. Los grupos externos abarcan clientes empresariales y minoristas, proveedores, accionistas, grupos industriales, asociaciones y la comunidad local, con iniciativas como encuestas, diálogos, productos sostenibles y reportes anuales alineados con principios de la ONU. Los resultados incluyen la integración de sostenibilidad en procesos de inversión, financiamiento verde, cumplimiento de códigos de conducta y apoyo a transformaciones sostenibles. Las metas están vinculadas a ESRS E1 y S1, y se alinean con la estrategia y modelo de negocio del banco.

  • ## Financial reporting ### Targets To support the realisation of Spar Nord's climate ambition of net zero by 2050, we have defined a number of 2030 sub-targets for decarbonisation of loan and investment activities and for the Bank's own operations. Additionally, Spar Nord has set sub-targets for selected segments, accompanied by specific actions and metrics, all designed to support the Bank's strategic direction. The reduction targets and sub-targets defined by the Bank are based on baseline analyses of the Bank's climate footprint through scope 1, 2 and 3. As the Bank's climate change initiatives are an on- going process, the baseline years are not identical across the three impact areas. However, the 2050 ambition is shared across the entire business, just as all activities have been assigned sub-targets for decarbonisation by 2030. Spar Nord's targets have been substantiated using scientific scenarios, which are described in more detail under the spe- cific activity.
  • The reduction targets for financed emissions from the Bank's core activities of loans and investments relate to significant shares of the Bank's business volume for bank and leasing loans and invest- ments in equities and corporate bonds in the Bank's asset management. The reduction targets related to the Bank's core activities are calculated in the relative metric tCO2e per DKK million, while the reduction targets for own operations are calculated in absolute emissions in the tCO2e metric. The illustration gives an overview of the Bank's cli- mate-related targets. For each target, the base- line years and the sub-targets set for 2025 and 2030 are presented. The target achievement by the end of 2024 illustrates progress relative to the Bank's 2030 targets measured on the basis of the relevant baseline year.
  • ## Financial reporting ### Asset management decarbonisation targets One-third of Spar Nord's GHG emissions is linked to the assets we manage on behalf of our customers. To support Spar Nord's net zero target, the Bank has defined a target of reducing financed emis- sions from investments in equities and corporate bonds in asset management by 30% by 2025 and 60% by 2030, respectively, relative to a 2020 baseline of 11.3 tCO2e per DKK million and based on scopes 1 and 2 for underlying businesses. To substantiate its sub-targets, the Bank has ap- plied the IPCC reduction pathway, which entails a minimum reduction of 48% in GHG emissions by 2030 and net zero by 2050 relative to 2019.   • ## Financial reporting ### Loan decarbonisation targets To support Spar Nord's net zero target, in 2022 the Bank defined two sub-targets for the reduction of financed emissions from lending activities to retail and business customers by 20% in 2025 and 45% in 2030, respectively, relative to a 2021 baseline of 8.8 tCO2e per DKK million. In 2024, Spar Nord de- cided to substantiate and refine its climate ambi- tion and the supporting reduction targets for fi- nanced emissions from lending activities by align- ing them with climate science-based net-zero sce- narios from the Intergovernmental Panel on Cli- mate Change (IPCC). This substantiation led to an adjustment of the sub-target for the overall loan portfolio from the previous reduction target of 45% to now 50% by 2030. Targets for reducing financed emissions (tCO2e per DKK million) from the overall loan portfolio % 100 80 60 40 20 0 2021 2024 2025 2030 Spar Nord Target IPCC pathway
  • % 100 80 60 40 20 0 2020 20242025 2030 Spar Nord Target IPCC pathway In 2024, financed emissions from investments in equities and corporate bonds in asset manage- ment, including investments in the asset classes through unit trust certificates, were reduced by 48% compared to the 2020 baseline. In 2024, fi- nanced emissions thus amounted to 5.9 tCO2e per DKK million. The positive developments in 2024 were attributa- ble in particular to lower financed emissions from investments in corporate bonds, which related both to conversion to more climate-friendly unit trust certificates and a reduction in emissions from existing unit trust certificates. The reduction means that the Bank has met the sub-target for 2025 and is well on its way to- wards meeting the 2030 target.
  • ### GHG emission reduction target (tCO2e) from scope 3 for own operations % 100 80 60 40 20 0 2021 2024 2030 Spar Nord Target / IPCC pathway In 2024, scope 3 GHG emissions from own opera- tions totalled 24,537 tCO2e, which, after a couple of years of falling numbers, is on a level with the 2021 baseline. The increase in 2024 was due to higher operating expenses because GHG emissions for the Bank's own operations are mainly calculated on the ba- sis of the monetary principle. It is generally Spar Nord's ambition to regularly increase the propor- tion of emissions calculated on the basis of pri- mary data in order to develop measures that will lead to a reduction of GHG emissions.

Je ne sais pas si les objectifs de réduction fixés par Spar Nord sont alignés avec une trajectoire de réchauffement à 1,5°C conformément aux Accords de Paris. Les documents fournis mentionnent que Spar Nord a aligné ses objectifs de réduction d'émissions avec des scénarios de réduction de l'IPCC, mais il n'est pas précisé si cela inclut une trajectoire conforme aux objectifs SBTi ou spécifiquement à une limitation du réchauffement à 1,5°C. Les informations sur l'alignement avec les recommandations de l'Accord de Paris ou les objectifs SBTi ne sont pas explicitement mentionnées dans le contexte fourni.

To support Spar Nord’s aspirations of net zero by 2050, the Bank has set a goal of reducing scope 1 and 2 GHG emissions by 30% by 2025 and 50% by 2030 compared to the 2021 baseline of 681 tCO2e. GHG emission reduction target (tCO2e) from scope 1 and 2 DKK million. The positive developments in 2024 were attributa-ble in particular to lower financed emissions from investments in corporate bonds, which related both to conversion to more climate- friendly unit trust certificates and a reduction in emissions from existing unit trust certificates. The reduction means that the Bank has met the sub- target for 2025 and is well on its way to- wards meeting the 2030 target. E1-6

Quels sont les leviers de décarbonation identifiés dans le plan de transition de l'entreprise ?

Pour répondre à cette question, nous souhaitons avoir la liste ou les noms des actions menées, accompagnées d'une description simple. Si possible, afficher les objectifs de réduction pour chacune des actions, avec l'année cible et l'année de référence.

1. Nom de l'action ou du projet de réduction.
2. Métrique.
3. Périmètre des émissions (Scope 1, 2 ou 3).
4. Année de référence.
5. Objectif de réduction.
6. Année cible. Des informations moins primordiales, mais souhaitables pourraient être :

- La méthodologie utilisée ou l'initiative correspondante.
- Les objectifs intermédiaires (2030, 2035, 2040, 2045).

Je suis désolé, mais les documents fournis ne contiennent pas de détails spécifiques sur les leviers de décarbonation ou sur le plan de transition de l'entreprise qui s'appliquent directement à votre question. Les informations disponibles se concentrent principalement sur les réductions globales des émissions de gaz à effet de serre (GES) et les objectifs climatiques généraux pour certaines catégories comme le prêt, le logement, le transport, et les investissements. Malheureusement, je ne peux pas fournir de liste détaillée ou de description des actions spécifiques de décarbonation.

Les leviers de décarbonation identifiés dans le plan de transition de Spar Nord incluent plusieurs actions stratégiques, chacune accompagnée de leurs propres objectifs de réduction. Voici une liste des actions menées :

  1. Réduction des émissions financées par le portefeuille de prêts

    • Métrique : tCO2e par DKK million
    • Périmètre des émissions : Scope 3
    • Année de référence : 2021
    • Objectif de réduction : 50% de réduction des émissions financées par le portefeuille de prêts d'ici 2030, par rapport à 2021
    • Méthodologie : Alignement avec les scénarios de réduction des émissions basés sur la science du Groupe d'experts intergouvernemental sur l'évolution du climat (GIEC).

  2. Augmentation des prêts pour véhicules électriques

    • Métrique : Nombre de prêts accordés
    • Périmètre des émissions : Scope 3
    • Année de référence : 2023
    • Objectif de réduction : Les nouveaux prêts pour véhicules électriques doivent représenter au moins 80% du total des prêts pour voitures d'ici 2030.
    • Méthodologie : Basé sur le chemin de réduction nette zéro pour le transport routier de l'Agence internationale de l'énergie (AIE).
    • Objectif intermédiaire : En 2024, les prêts pour véhicules électriques représentaient déjà 60% des prêts totaux pour voitures.

  3. Transition vers l'énergie renouvelable

    • Métrique : Consommation d'énergie
    • Périmètre des émissions : Scope 2
    • Année de référence : 2023
    • Objectif de réduction : Consommation d'électricité provenant à 100% de sources renouvelables, à partir de 2023 sur une période de dix ans.
    • Méthodologie : Partenariat avec Better Energy et production propre à partir de panneaux solaires.

  4. Conversion de la flotte de véhicules de l'entreprise vers l'électrique

    • Métrique : Pourcentage de véhicules électriques
    • Périmètre des émissions : Scope 1
    • Année de référence : Non spécifiée
    • Objectif de réduction : 80% des besoins en transport du personnel couverts par des voitures électriques d'ici 2030, avec tous les nouveaux véhicules achetés étant exclusivement électriques.
    • Objectif intermédiaire : Aucun spécifié dans le contexte.

Ces actions sont conçues pour aligner les efforts de Spar Nord avec l'Accord de Paris, visant à limiter le réchauffement climatique à 1,5°C.

  • ## Financial reporting ### Targets To support the realisation of Spar Nord's climate ambition of net zero by 2050, we have defined a number of 2030 sub-targets for decarbonisation of loan and investment activities and for the Bank's own operations. Additionally, Spar Nord has set sub-targets for selected segments, accompanied by specific actions and metrics, all designed to support the Bank's strategic direction. The reduction targets and sub-targets defined by the Bank are based on baseline analyses of the Bank's climate footprint through scope 1, 2 and 3. As the Bank's climate change initiatives are an on- going process, the baseline years are not identical across the three impact areas. However, the 2050 ambition is shared across the entire business, just as all activities have been assigned sub-targets for decarbonisation by 2030. Spar Nord's targets have been substantiated using scientific scenarios, which are described in more detail under the spe- cific activity.

  • Spar Nord's climate targets for 2030, based on various baselines, include significant reductions in financed emissions and increased green financing. For lending, emissions must decrease by 20% by 2025 and 50% by 2030 relative to a 2021 baseline of 8.8 tCO2e per DKKm. By 2030, 80% of new car loans must be for electric cars (2023 baseline: 41%), and financed emissions from private housing and transport must drop by 70% (2023 baseline: 11.4 kgCO2e/m²/year) and 30% (2023 baseline: 40.7 tCO2e per DKKm), respectively. Green financing linked to the Bank's Green Bond Framework must reach DKK 10 billion by 2030, while emissions from investments in equities and corporate bonds must decline by 30% by 2025 and 60% by 2030 (2020 baseline: 11.3 tCO2e per DKKm). For the Bank's own operations, scope 1 and 2 emissions must reduce by 30% by 2025 and 50% by 2030 (2021 baseline: 681 tCO2e), and scope 3 emissions must decrease by 25% by 2030 (2021 baseline: 24,748 tCO2e).

G1-41

Quelle est la valeur monétaire des contributions politiques, financières et en nature apportées directement et indirectement par l'entreprise ? Distinguer le montant total des contributions financières directes, des contributions financières indirectes et des contributions en nature.

Contexte: Pour cette question, nous analysons les activités et politiques de lobbying de l'entreprise. On entend par « contribution politique », l'aide financière ou en nature apportée directement aux partis politiques, à leurs représentants élus ou aux personnes qui briguent une fonction politique. Les contributions financières incluent les dons, les prêts, les parrainages, les avances pour services, ou l'achat de billets pour des événements de collecte de fonds et d'autres pratiques similaires.
Les contributions en nature incluent la publication, l'utilisation d'installations, la conception et l'impression, le don de matériel, l'adhésion à un conseil d'administration, l'emploi ou le travail de consultance pour des responsables politiques élus ou des candidats à un mandat.
Par « contribution politique indirecte », on entend les contributions politiques apportées par l'intermédiaire d'une organisation (de lobbying ou caritative par exemple) ou l'aide apportée à une organisation, par exemple un groupe de réflexion ou une organisation professionnelle proche de certains partis ou de certaines causes politiques, ou qui soutient ces partis/causes.

Consignes: Distinguer le montant total des contributions financières directes, des contributions financières indirectes et des contributions en nature.
Pour chaque type de contribution, indiquer si les données sont disponibles, ainsi que le pays ou la zone géographique et le bénéficiaire de la contribution.
Présenter les données sous forme de tableau, avec les années et les montants respectifs.
Veuillez noter que si ces valeurs ne sont pas affichées, cela peut être interprété comme un signe que l'entreprise ne verse pas de contributions politiques ou d'autres contributions financières liées à l'influence et aux pratiques de lobbying.

Je suis désolé, mais les informations concernant les contributions politiques, financières et en nature de l'entreprise, qu'elles soient directes ou indirectes, ne sont pas disponibles dans les documents fournis. Par conséquent, je ne peux pas distinguer les montants totaux des différentes contributions ni indiquer les pays ou zones géographiques concernés. Si ces valeurs ne sont pas affichées, cela peut être interprété comme un signe que l'entreprise ne verse pas de contributions politiques ou d'autres contributions financières liées à l'influence et aux pratiques de lobbying.

  • Le tableau détaille les catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent : **Goods and services**, **Capital goods**, **Fuel- and energy-related activities**, **Upstream transportation and distribution**, **Waste generated in operations**, **Business travel**, **Employee commuting**, et **Upstream leased assets**. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, avec des données basées sur des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme **Upstream leased assets**, sont jugées non pertinentes car leurs émissions sont incluses dans les scopes 1 et 2. Les calculs utilisent des sources variées, telles que les données des fournisseurs, les bases de données DEFRA et Exiobase, ainsi que les statistiques nationales. and

    BEGIN TABLE

    Scope 3 category Description of category Assessment of relevance Description of underlying data
    Goods and services Emissions associated with the extraction, production and transportation of goods and services purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are mainly based on the monetary principle on the operating costs for the year. Data processing is performed at the account level. In some places, the monetary principle has been replaced by emission data from the supplier. Spar Nord calculates emissions related to BEC based on the supplier’s emission data and uses the Bank’s share of BEC for BEC’s scope 1 and 2 emissions. Water consumption is disclosed on the basis of meter readings at locations where Spar Nord has its own water meters.
    Capital goods Emissions associated with the extraction of materials for and the production and transportation of capital goods purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are based on the monetary principle based on purchasing data of assets acquired during the relevant year.
    Fuel- and energy-related activities Emissions associated with the extraction, production, and transportation of fuels and energy purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year, not already accounted for in scope 1 or scope 2. The category is considered relevant. Data have already been collected for scope 1 and 2. Calculated on the basis of the same physical consumption data applied for calculating scope 1 and 2 emissions. - Upstream emissions from electricity are calculated on the basis of distribution loss and the distribution of the power grid energy sources from Energinet and IPCC. - Upstream emissions from district heating are calculated on the basis of distribution losses calculated from Energinet. - Upstream emissions from natural gas are calculated based on distribution losses. - Upstream emissions from diesel and petrol consumption are calculated on the basis of extraction, production and transportation of fuels compiled from DEFRA.
    Upstream transportation and distribution Emissions associated with the transportation and distribution of goods purchased by the reporting company in the reporting year in vehicles not owned or controlled by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. However, emissions from this category cannot be separated from categories 1 and 2 due to the lack of supplier data. The emissions are thus presented in categories 1 and 2.
    Waste generated in operations Emissions associated with the disposal and treatment of waste generated in the reporting company’s operations in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data are compiled for the Bank’s headquarters and other Spar Nord locations where data are available. Waste volumes have been obtained from waste contractors in physical amounts. According to the GHG Protocol, the allocation principle ‘recycled content method’ is applied. Emissions associated with waste are calculated at 0, as the waste fractions are sent for further processing.
    Business travel Emissions from the transportation of employees for business-related activities during the reporting year in vehicles not owned or operated by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. Emission factors for the calculation have been obtained from the Exiobase database. Employee air travel is primarily based on CO2 calculations provided by travel agencies. In the calculation of emissions, a distinction is made between domestic and international flights, using relevant emission factors from DEFRA without RFI. Travel in employees’ private vehicles is based on recorded mileage. Emission factors are based on calculations from the Danish Centre for Environment and Energy (DCE) on passenger transport by means of transport and DEFRA.
    Employee commuting Emissions from the transportation of employees between their homes and their worksites during the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data on employee private commuting are based on estimates calculated using Statistics Denmark data on travel patterns, number of employees in the relevant year, and emissions factors from the Danish Energy Agency and DEFRA.
    Upstream leased assets Emissions from the operation of assets leased by the reporting company in the reporting year and not included in scope 1 and scope 2. The category is not considered relevant because emissions from leased buildings and leased vehicles are included in scope 1 and 2 in accordance with the selected consolidation approach.

    Résumé du contenu du tableau : Le tableau présente les différentes catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent les biens et services, les biens d'équipement, les activités liées aux combustibles et à l'énergie, le transport et la distribution en amont, les déchets générés par les opérations, les déplacements professionnels, les trajets domicile-travail des employés et les actifs loués en amont. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, et les données utilisées pour les calculs sont détaillées, incluant des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme les actifs loués en amont, sont jugées non pertinentes.

Je ne sais pas. Les valeurs monétaires des contributions politiques, financières et en nature apportées directement ou indirectement par l'entreprise ne sont pas mentionnées dans les documents fournis. Selon le contexte disponible, Spar Nord ne fait aucune contribution financière pour exercer une influence politique, ni ne souhaite être associée à une orientation politique spécifique. Cela pourrait être interprété comme un signe que l'entreprise ne verse pas de contributions politiques ou d'autres contributions financières liées à l'influence et aux pratiques de lobbying.

  • ### Political influence and lobbying activities In line with its corporate social responsibility and local commitment, the Bank continuously provides financial contributions and sponsorships to a wide range of causes and organisations in the towns and areas where we operate. Spar Nord is a mem- ber of the industry communities National Banks in Denmark and Finance Denmark, both of which aim to promote the interests of banks in the public de- bate and to increase knowledge and confidence in the financial sector in general. None of Spar Nord's sponsorships or memberships are moti- vated by an intention to exercise party political influence, nor does the Bank make any financial contribution to, or wish to be associated with, a specific political direction.

Je ne dispose pas des informations sur la valeur monétaire des contributions politiques, financières et en nature apportées directement et indirectement par l'entreprise. Selon le contexte fourni, Spar Nord ne fait pas de contributions financières à des partis politiques ni n'exerce d'influence politique par le biais de ses parrainages ou adhésions. Par conséquent, il n'y a pas de données disponibles concernant les montants des contributions politiques directes, indirectes ou en nature pour Spar Nord. Cela peut être interprété comme un signe que l'entreprise ne verse pas de contributions politiques ou d'autres contributions financières liées à l'influence et aux pratiques de lobbying.

Spar Nord a mis en place plusieurs mesures pour remédier au non-respect des procédures et des normes en matière de lutte contre la corruption. Voici un résumé des actions principales :

  1. Politique de Tolérance Zéro : Spar Nord applique une politique de tolérance zéro envers la corruption et la bribery, tant en interne qu'en collaboration avec ses clients et partenaires externes (Context Num-5).

  2. Formation Obligatoire : Tous les employés reçoivent une formation obligatoire sur la lutte contre la corruption et la bribery pour illustrer où ils doivent faire preuve d'une attention accrue (Context Num-4).

  3. Contrôles Renforcés : Des contrôles accrus sont effectués sur les employés particulièrement exposés à la corruption, notamment ceux du département AML et les membres du conseil exécutif. Cela inclut l'obtention de casiers judiciaires annuels conformément à la loi danoise sur la lutte contre le blanchiment d'argent (Context Num-5).

  4. Environnement de Contrôle Préventif : La banque a mis en place un ensemble de mesures préventives et un environnement de contrôle pour atténuer la corruption et la bribery, notamment en ce qui concerne les cadeaux, dons, conflits d'intérêts, et les risques liés aux transactions avec des tiers (Context Num-3).

  5. Sensibilisation et Code de Conduite : Pour accroître la sensibilisation des employés, Spar Nord a développé une politique anti-corruption et un code de conduite qui décrivent les attentes en matière de comportement éthique (Context Num-4).

Ces mesures témoignent de l'engagement continu de Spar Nord en matière de lutte anti-corruption, visant à assurer l'intégrité personnelle et organisationnelle.

  • La tabla detalla la organización y resultados del compromiso de Spar Nord con grupos de interés internos y externos en 2024. Los grupos internos incluyen el Consejo de Administración, la Junta Ejecutiva, el grupo de dirección ESG, el Comité de Inversión Responsable, el Comité de Finanzas Sostenibles y los empleados, con actividades como reuniones trimestrales, talleres y consultas, enfocadas en metas de sostenibilidad, gobernanza y desarrollo de productos responsables. Los grupos externos abarcan clientes empresariales y minoristas, proveedores, accionistas, grupos industriales, asociaciones y la comunidad local, con iniciativas como encuestas, diálogos, productos sostenibles y reportes anuales alineados con principios de la ONU. Los resultados incluyen la integración de sostenibilidad en procesos de inversión, financiamiento verde, cumplimiento de códigos de conducta y apoyo a transformaciones sostenibles. Las metas están vinculadas a ESRS E1 y S1, y se alinean con la estrategia y modelo de negocio del banco.
  • To reduce the risk of the Bank's employees, cus- tomers, or partners being exposed to or engaging in corruption and bribery, the Bank has imple- mented a range of preventive measures and es- tablished a control environment designed to miti- gate corruption and bribery associated with vari- ous elements, such as gifts, donations, conflicts of interest, third-party providers, and customer-re- lated transaction risks. In addition, the Bank's em- ployees, including the Board of Directors and Exec- utive Board, and other management layers, are screened to determine whether they are, or have been, related to a politically exposed person. Fur- thermore, monitoring of employees' accounts is conducted. At the end of 2024, the Bank has not received any convictions or fines related to corruption and brib- ery, nor has there been any incidents in this re- gard, which is also stated in the memo on Man- agement statement on fraud, which is discussed annually by the Board of Directors.
  • ## Financial reporting policy should be read in conjunction with the Bank's internal staff handbook, which elaborates on how employees should act in connection with potential conflicts of interest, receipt and giving of gifts, entertainment, invitations, business part- ners, close relations, etc. To increase employee awareness and equip them as well as possible in relation to corruption and bribery, all employees and all customers go through the obligations under the money launder- ing regulations. Employees also receive manda- tory training in anti-corruption and bribery to ex- emplify where they need to show increased atten- tion.
  • The table from the Spar Nord Annual Report 2024 outlines sustainability topics, their value chain impacts, descriptions, and related policies/measures. For "Corporate culture," the Bank ensures a sound corporate culture ("Positive impact," "Own operations") supported by a "Policy on sound corporate culture." Regarding "Protection of whistleblowers," the Bank's whistleblower scheme ("Positive impact," "Own operations") is backed by a "Whistleblower policy." Risks such as corruption and bribery ("Own operations"), money laundering and terrorist financing ("Own operations"), fraud ("Downstream"), information security ("Own operations"), and data governance ("Own operations") are addressed through respective policies, including "Anti-corruption and bribery policy," "AML policies," "Governance documents and processes," "Information security policy," and "Data governance policy." Additionally, the Bank ensures timely supplier payments ("Positive impact," "Upstream") supported by governance documents and processes.
  • · Policy on training and screening of AML em- ployees · Policy on transaction monitoring and sanction screening The policies are approved by the Executive Board and Board of Directors, ensuring that the Bank's AML efforts are anchored at the highest levels of management. The efforts against money laundering, terrorist fi- nancing and other financial crimes are a major fo- cus within Spar Nord, and it is therefore important that all management levels are knowledgeable about and informed of the specific initiatives in this area. For this reason, quarterly reporting is made to both the Executive Board and the Audit Committee and at least half-yearly to the Board of Directors, which ensures that the Bank's highest Level of management is informed of developments in the area.
  • ### Anti-corruption and bribery At Spar Nord, we have a zero tolerance policy to- wards corruption and bribery. This applies both in- ternally at Spar Nord and in cooperation with our customers and external partners. In general, Spar Nord estimates that all employees are exposed to corruption and bribery. However, employees in the AML department, key persons and the members of the Bank's Executive Board are particularly ex- posed, which is why the Bank carries out increased checks on these persons, which, among other things, involves obtaining criminal records on an annual basis according to the Danish AML Act.
  • Internal processes have been established for re- porting work-related accidents, threats and ha- rassment. Annual follow-up and evaluation of re- ported incidents is carried out under the auspices of the working environment committee. The bank also has a whistleblower scheme, which is an independent and autonomous channel through which an employee can report concerns or potential violations of financial legislation com- mitted by the Bank, its employees, or members of the Board of Directors. For a more detailed de- scription of the Bank's whistleblower scheme, see the section G1 Business conduct.
  • In order for the Bank to maintain the highest standard of personal and organisational integrity and prudence and to minimise risks, it is important that Spar Nord's employees are familiar with the conduct and work ethics expected of them. There- fore, Spar Nord has developed an anti-corruption and bribery policy describing the expectations management has of the Bank's employees. The Spar Nord Annual Report 2024 102

Les mesures prises pour remédier au non-respect des procédures et des normes en matière de lutte contre la corruption incluent l'implémentation d'une politique de tolérance zéro envers la corruption et le pot-de-vin, qui s'applique tant en interne qu'en coopération avec les clients et partenaires externes (Context Num-7). Pour détecter et prévenir la corruption, le personnel de Spar Nord, y compris ses cadres, est soumis à un contrôle accru, notamment par le biais de vérifications annuelles des antécédents criminels conformément à la loi danoise sur la lutte contre le blanchiment d'argent (Context Num-7). De plus, des formations obligatoires sur la lutte contre la corruption et la prévention du blanchiment d'argent sont dispensées aux employés pour accroître leur sensibilisation et leurs compétences dans ces domaines (Context Num-4). Ces efforts sont soutenus par des politiques internes approuvées par le Conseil d'administration et la Direction générale, garantissant que les efforts de lutte contre le blanchiment d'argent et la corruption sont ancrés au plus haut niveau de la gestion de la banque (Context Num-6).

  • Spar Nord prioritises maintaining good and trans- parent supplier relationships that underpin the Bank’s good reputation and help attract and retain good suppliers and customers. Spar Nord re-quires that the Bank’s suppliers support interna- tionally recognised principles for human rights, the International Labour Organization labour market conventions on the dignity of workers, as well as the UN Sustainable Development Goals and the ten general principles described in the UN Global Compact. Spar Nord has prepar ed a code of conduct for suppliers, and all of the Bank’s pri- mary suppliers automatically accede to this when they either establish or renew supplier agreements with the Bank. In 2024, Spar Nord selected 25 suppliers and asked them in a questionnaire to consider the spe-cific circumstances in their own supply chain and production. Their responses were generally satis- factory, and only very few gave rise to further scrutiny and dia logue. In addition to addressing specific tasks, the Bank must be able to handle the constantly evolving threat landscape within this area. This places great demands on knowledge, systems and em-
  • mental Principles and Rights at Work or the OECD Guidelines for Multinational Enterprises.   • Le tableau détaille les catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent : **Goods and services**, **Capital goods**, **Fuel- and energy-related activities**, **Upstream transportation and distribution**, **Waste generated in operations**, **Business travel**, **Employee commuting**, et **Upstream leased assets**. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, avec des données basées sur des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme **Upstream leased assets**, sont jugées non pertinentes car leurs émissions sont incluses dans les scopes 1 et 2. Les calculs utilisent des sources variées, telles que les données des fournisseurs, les bases de données DEFRA et Exiobase, ainsi que les statistiques nationales. and

    BEGIN TABLE

    Scope 3 category Description of category Assessment of relevance Description of underlying data
    Goods and services Emissions associated with the extraction, production and transportation of goods and services purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are mainly based on the monetary principle on the operating costs for the year. Data processing is performed at the account level. In some places, the monetary principle has been replaced by emission data from the supplier. Spar Nord calculates emissions related to BEC based on the supplier’s emission data and uses the Bank’s share of BEC for BEC’s scope 1 and 2 emissions. Water consumption is disclosed on the basis of meter readings at locations where Spar Nord has its own water meters.
    Capital goods Emissions associated with the extraction of materials for and the production and transportation of capital goods purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are based on the monetary principle based on purchasing data of assets acquired during the relevant year.
    Fuel- and energy-related activities Emissions associated with the extraction, production, and transportation of fuels and energy purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year, not already accounted for in scope 1 or scope 2. The category is considered relevant. Data have already been collected for scope 1 and 2. Calculated on the basis of the same physical consumption data applied for calculating scope 1 and 2 emissions. - Upstream emissions from electricity are calculated on the basis of distribution loss and the distribution of the power grid energy sources from Energinet and IPCC. - Upstream emissions from district heating are calculated on the basis of distribution losses calculated from Energinet. - Upstream emissions from natural gas are calculated based on distribution losses. - Upstream emissions from diesel and petrol consumption are calculated on the basis of extraction, production and transportation of fuels compiled from DEFRA.
    Upstream transportation and distribution Emissions associated with the transportation and distribution of goods purchased by the reporting company in the reporting year in vehicles not owned or controlled by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. However, emissions from this category cannot be separated from categories 1 and 2 due to the lack of supplier data. The emissions are thus presented in categories 1 and 2.
    Waste generated in operations Emissions associated with the disposal and treatment of waste generated in the reporting company’s operations in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data are compiled for the Bank’s headquarters and other Spar Nord locations where data are available. Waste volumes have been obtained from waste contractors in physical amounts. According to the GHG Protocol, the allocation principle ‘recycled content method’ is applied. Emissions associated with waste are calculated at 0, as the waste fractions are sent for further processing.
    Business travel Emissions from the transportation of employees for business-related activities during the reporting year in vehicles not owned or operated by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. Emission factors for the calculation have been obtained from the Exiobase database. Employee air travel is primarily based on CO2 calculations provided by travel agencies. In the calculation of emissions, a distinction is made between domestic and international flights, using relevant emission factors from DEFRA without RFI. Travel in employees’ private vehicles is based on recorded mileage. Emission factors are based on calculations from the Danish Centre for Environment and Energy (DCE) on passenger transport by means of transport and DEFRA.
    Employee commuting Emissions from the transportation of employees between their homes and their worksites during the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data on employee private commuting are based on estimates calculated using Statistics Denmark data on travel patterns, number of employees in the relevant year, and emissions factors from the Danish Energy Agency and DEFRA.
    Upstream leased assets Emissions from the operation of assets leased by the reporting company in the reporting year and not included in scope 1 and scope 2. The category is not considered relevant because emissions from leased buildings and leased vehicles are included in scope 1 and 2 in accordance with the selected consolidation approach.

    Résumé du contenu du tableau : Le tableau présente les différentes catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent les biens et services, les biens d'équipement, les activités liées aux combustibles et à l'énergie, le transport et la distribution en amont, les déchets générés par les opérations, les déplacements professionnels, les trajets domicile-travail des employés et les actifs loués en amont. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, et les données utilisées pour les calculs sont détaillées, incluant des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme les actifs loués en amont, sont jugées non pertinentes.

  • Le tableau détaille les catégories d'émissions Scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence pour la banque, et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories "Downstream transportation and distribution", "Processing of sold products", "Use of sold products", "End-of-life treatment of sold products" et "Franchises" ne sont pas pertinentes car la banque ne vend pas de produits physiques ni ne possède de franchises. Les catégories "Downstream leased assets" et "Investments" sont jugées pertinentes. Les émissions des actifs loués en aval sont estimées à partir de la consommation énergétique des propriétés louées, tandis que celles des investissements et des prêts sont calculées selon le modèle CO2 de Finance Denmark, en utilisant des données sectorielles et spécifiques aux types d'actifs. Les calculs incluent les émissions des portefeuilles d'actifs, des prêts aux clients, et des propriétés ou véhicules financés. and

    BEGIN TABLE

    Scope 3 category Description of category Assessment of relevance Description of underlying data
    Downstream transportation and distribution Emissions from the transportation and distribution of products sold. The category is not considered relevant because the Bank does not sell physical products.
    Processing of sold products Emissions from the processing of intermediate products sold in the reporting year by downstream companies. The category is not considered relevant because the Bank does not sell physical products.
    Use of sold products End use of goods and services sold by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is not considered relevant because the Bank does not sell physical products.
    End-of-life treatment of sold products Emissions from the disposal and treatment of waste from products sold by the reporting company in the reporting year at the end of their life. The category is not considered relevant because the Bank does not sell physical products.
    Downstream leased assets Emissions from the operation of assets owned by the reporting company and leased in the reporting year, not included in scope 1 and scope 2. The category is considered relevant. The energy consumption of let properties is estimated on the basis of calculated key energy consumption figures per square metre area (based on the Bank’s owned square metres) and the number of square metres let in the relevant year. Emission factors are the same as those used in calculating scope 1 and 2 and scope 3, category 3.
    Franchises Emissions from the operation of franchises in the reporting year, not included in scope 1 and scope 2. The category is not considered relevant because the Bank does not own franchises.
    Investments Emissions from investments, including asset management and proprietary portfolio, as well as loans to retail and business customers. The category is considered relevant. GHG emissions associated with the Bank’s lending and investments are calculated in accordance with Finance Denmark’s CO2 model.

    Lending: The calculation of financed absolute and relative emissions from lending is based on the Bank’s lending at year-end, calculated before impairment charges. The calculation only includes loans recognised in the balance sheet and thus does not include mediated loans where the loans are recognised in the balance sheet of a collaborating bank such as Totalkredit and DLR Kredit. Reverse transactions are not included in the calculation basis. The loan consists of bank loans and leasing loans. Leasing activities include financial leasing where the lessee acquires control of the asset after the lease expires, and the related emissions are therefore presented together with the Bank’s other loans in category 15. The calculation of financed absolute and relative emissions from bank and leasing loans to business customers is based on an industry breakdown of the loan portfolio, and the emission factors are based on data from Statistics Denmark. Emissions from home loans are estimated on the basis of the buildings’ energy performance certificate, and where there is no such certificate, the estimate is based on other knowledge about the individual property. For car loans to retail customers, WLTP emission factors are used based on the fuel type of the specific vehicle. Emissions cover scope 1 and 2 emissions.

    Investments: The calculation of financed absolute and relative emissions from investments was made on the basis of the Bank’s investments in Spar Nord’s asset management and proprietary portfolio. Investments where the Bank has the decision-making authority are included in the calculation. This means the calculation also includes holdings that are not part of the Bank’s financial balance sheet, such as Stjerneinvest and individual power of attorney agreements. The calculation includes investments in equities, corporate bonds, unit trusts, mortgage bonds and ship mortgage bonds. For equities, corporate bonds and unit trusts, emission data from MSCI is used; for mortgage bonds data from Capital Market Partners is used, and for ship mortgage bonds data from Danmarks Skibskredit A/S is used. The calculation covers scope 1 and 2 emissions for the shipyards and also scope 3 emissions.

    Résumé du tableau : Le tableau présente différentes catégories d'émissions de type Scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence pour la banque, et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories liées à la vente de produits physiques (transport, traitement, utilisation, fin de vie) et aux franchises ne sont pas pertinentes car la banque ne vend pas de produits physiques ni ne possède de franchises. En revanche, les émissions liées aux actifs loués en aval et aux investissements sont jugées pertinentes. Les émissions des actifs loués sont calculées sur la base de la consommation énergétique des propriétés louées. Les émissions des investissements et des prêts sont calculées selon le modèle CO2 de Finance Denmark, en tenant compte des portefeuilles d'actifs, des prêts aux clients et des données spécifiques aux secteurs et aux types d'actifs.

  • In relation to scope 3 GHG emissions, 8 of the 15 scope 3 categories are relevant for Spar Nord for calculating emissions. Of these, 7 categories con- cern emissions relating to own operations, while category 15 relates to the Bank's core activities of lending and investments. Emissions in categories 1, 2, 3, 5, 6, 7 and 13, which all relate to the Bank's own operations, totalled 24,537 tCO2e in 2024, against 22,066 in 2023. This 11% increase was pri- marily attributable to category 1 Purchased goods and services and 2 Capital goods. GHG emissions for the Bank's own operations are mainly com- piled on the basis of the monetary principle, and only 1,642 tCO2e, equal to 6%, were compiled on the basis of primary data. The development in scope 3 emissions thus widely reflects the increase in costs in 2024 relative to 2023.

  • ### Financial reporting The table outlines Spar Nord's **Scope 3 emissions categories** for the reporting year, detailing their **descriptions**, **relevance assessments**, and **underlying data**. Categories 1 (Goods and services) and 2 (Capital goods) are deemed relevant, with emissions calculated primarily using the monetary principle, supplemented by supplier data where available. Categories 3 (Fuel- and energy-related activities), 5 (Waste generated in operations), 6 (Business travel), and 7 (Employee commuting) are also considered relevant, with emissions calculated using specific data sources such as Energinet, DEFRA, Exiobase, and Statistics Denmark. The report highlights Spar Nord's reliance on external data sources and methodologies, such as BEC Financial Technologies and waste contractors, for accurate emissions reporting.

  • ### GHG Emissions Spar Nord's compilation of GHG emissions has been prepared in accordance with the regulations of E1 Climate change, which refers to the GHG Pro- tocol. The compilation also builds on Finance Denmark's CO2 model for the financial sector, which is based on PCAF's methods and the GHG Protocol. · Scope 1 covers direct emissions derived from the Bank's activities and processes, including fuel consumption in the Bank's vehicles and fuel for heating. · Scope 2 covers indirect emissions from produc- tion of the energy consumed by the Bank from the public utility grid, including electricity and district heating. · Scope 3 covers indirect emissions from the up- stream and downstream value chain. GHG emissions derive from, among other things, ex- traction of raw materials, transportation and production of the materials, goods and services consumed by the Bank. Indirect emissions re- lated to the Bank's lending and investment are also included here.
  • GHG emissions from the Bank's own operations In 2024, extensive efforts were undertaken to im- prove the completeness of the compilation of the Bank's GHG emissions for the Bank's own opera- tions. We have thus formalised the calculation processes and have added a calculation for re- maining material scope 3 categories. As a result, the comparative figures for earlier years have been restated to the principles and methods ap- plied in 2024. As a result of the updated principles and methods, GHG emissions from own operations have increased sharply compared with previously. Recalculations have been made for all the com- parative years in order to report quantitative data that are consistent over time.

Les émissions totales du Scope 2, calculées grâce à la méthode "location-based", sont de 784 tCO2e en 2024.

  • 74 Spar Nord Annual Report 2024 GHG emissions Spar Nord calculates GHG emissions pursuant to E1 Climate change, which refers to the three scopes of the GHG Protocol, where a distinction is made between direct and indirect GHG emissions. Spar Nord’s direct greenhouse gas emissions are generated through the Bank’s own operations from driving the Bank’s cars and heating with nat-ural gas and are calculated in scope 1. The Bank’s indirect GHG emissions from consumed electricity and district heating are calculated in scope 2. The Bank's other indirect GHG emissions relate both to its own banking operations and in particu- lar to its core lending and investment activities and are calculated in scope 3. Indirect GHG emissions from own operations are particularly related to the purchase of goods and services, as well as business travel and staff com- muting to and from work.   • Le tableau détaille les catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent : **Goods and services**, **Capital goods**, **Fuel- and energy-related activities**, **Upstream transportation and distribution**, **Waste generated in operations**, **Business travel**, **Employee commuting**, et **Upstream leased assets**. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, avec des données basées sur des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme **Upstream leased assets**, sont jugées non pertinentes car leurs émissions sont incluses dans les scopes 1 et 2. Les calculs utilisent des sources variées, telles que les données des fournisseurs, les bases de données DEFRA et Exiobase, ainsi que les statistiques nationales. and

    BEGIN TABLE

    Scope 3 category Description of category Assessment of relevance Description of underlying data
    Goods and services Emissions associated with the extraction, production and transportation of goods and services purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are mainly based on the monetary principle on the operating costs for the year. Data processing is performed at the account level. In some places, the monetary principle has been replaced by emission data from the supplier. Spar Nord calculates emissions related to BEC based on the supplier’s emission data and uses the Bank’s share of BEC for BEC’s scope 1 and 2 emissions. Water consumption is disclosed on the basis of meter readings at locations where Spar Nord has its own water meters.
    Capital goods Emissions associated with the extraction of materials for and the production and transportation of capital goods purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant in view of the extent of the Bank’s purchases. The calculated emissions are based on the monetary principle based on purchasing data of assets acquired during the relevant year.
    Fuel- and energy-related activities Emissions associated with the extraction, production, and transportation of fuels and energy purchased or acquired by the reporting company in the reporting year, not already accounted for in scope 1 or scope 2. The category is considered relevant. Data have already been collected for scope 1 and 2. Calculated on the basis of the same physical consumption data applied for calculating scope 1 and 2 emissions. - Upstream emissions from electricity are calculated on the basis of distribution loss and the distribution of the power grid energy sources from Energinet and IPCC. - Upstream emissions from district heating are calculated on the basis of distribution losses calculated from Energinet. - Upstream emissions from natural gas are calculated based on distribution losses. - Upstream emissions from diesel and petrol consumption are calculated on the basis of extraction, production and transportation of fuels compiled from DEFRA.
    Upstream transportation and distribution Emissions associated with the transportation and distribution of goods purchased by the reporting company in the reporting year in vehicles not owned or controlled by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. However, emissions from this category cannot be separated from categories 1 and 2 due to the lack of supplier data. The emissions are thus presented in categories 1 and 2.
    Waste generated in operations Emissions associated with the disposal and treatment of waste generated in the reporting company’s operations in the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data are compiled for the Bank’s headquarters and other Spar Nord locations where data are available. Waste volumes have been obtained from waste contractors in physical amounts. According to the GHG Protocol, the allocation principle ‘recycled content method’ is applied. Emissions associated with waste are calculated at 0, as the waste fractions are sent for further processing.
    Business travel Emissions from the transportation of employees for business-related activities during the reporting year in vehicles not owned or operated by the reporting company. The category is considered relevant. Emission factors for the calculation have been obtained from the Exiobase database. Employee air travel is primarily based on CO2 calculations provided by travel agencies. In the calculation of emissions, a distinction is made between domestic and international flights, using relevant emission factors from DEFRA without RFI. Travel in employees’ private vehicles is based on recorded mileage. Emission factors are based on calculations from the Danish Centre for Environment and Energy (DCE) on passenger transport by means of transport and DEFRA.
    Employee commuting Emissions from the transportation of employees between their homes and their worksites during the reporting year. The category is considered relevant. Data on employee private commuting are based on estimates calculated using Statistics Denmark data on travel patterns, number of employees in the relevant year, and emissions factors from the Danish Energy Agency and DEFRA.
    Upstream leased assets Emissions from the operation of assets leased by the reporting company in the reporting year and not included in scope 1 and scope 2. The category is not considered relevant because emissions from leased buildings and leased vehicles are included in scope 1 and 2 in accordance with the selected consolidation approach.

    Résumé du contenu du tableau : Le tableau présente les différentes catégories d'émissions de scope 3, leur description, leur pertinence et les données sous-jacentes utilisées pour les calculs. Les catégories incluent les biens et services, les biens d'équipement, les activités liées aux combustibles et à l'énergie, le transport et la distribution en amont, les déchets générés par les opérations, les déplacements professionnels, les trajets domicile-travail des employés et les actifs loués en amont. Chaque catégorie est évaluée en termes de pertinence, et les données utilisées pour les calculs sont détaillées, incluant des principes monétaires, des données physiques, des facteurs d'émission et des méthodes spécifiques. Certaines catégories, comme les actifs loués en amont, sont jugées non pertinentes.

  • Le tableau présente les émissions de CO2 équivalent (tCO2e) pour les opérations propres sur trois années : 2023, 2022 et 2021. - Les émissions selon le "Previous reporting" étaient de 1,944 tCO2e en 2023, 2,906 tCO2e en 2022 et 2,683 tCO2e en 2021. - Les émissions révisées pour 2024 ("Reporting in 2024") montrent une augmentation significative, atteignant 22,681 tCO2e en 2023, 22,638 tCO2e en 2022 et 25,429 tCO2e en 2021. - Les "Total changes for own operations" s’élèvent à 20,737 tCO2e en 2023, 19,732 tCO2e en 2022 et 22,746 tCO2e en 2021. and
